## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: solid mechanics / materials constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task belongs to constitutive modeling of materials, where stress (sigma) is expressed as a function of strain (epsilon) and temperature (T). The physical relationship typically includes elastic behavior, plastic hardening, and thermal softening effects, often represented by separable or coupled functional forms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear thermoelastic: sigma = c0 * (1 - c1 * T) * epsilon (temperature-dependent elastic modulus at small strain)
- Hollomon hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (isothermal power‑law plastic flow stress)
- Ludwik hardening: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power‑law strain hardening)
- Swift hardening with prestrain: sigma = c0 * (c1 + epsilon)**c2 (offset power‑law hardening, prestrain effect)
- Voce saturation hardening: sigma = c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(-c2 * epsilon)) (exponential saturation of flow stress)
- Simplified Johnson–Cook: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - c3 * T) (combined hardening and linear thermal softening)
- Multiplicative exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(-c2 * T) (power‑law hardening with exponential thermal decay)
- Coupled power‑law: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * T**c2 (power‑law scaling in both strain and temperature)
- Ramberg–Osgood smooth curve: sigma = c0 * epsilon / (1 + (c1 * epsilon)**c2)**(1/c2) (smooth elastic–plastic transition)
- Quadratic nonlinear elastic: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 (low‑order polynomial hardening)
- Thermally‑softened yield with power‑law: sigma = c0 * (1 - c1 * T) + c2 * epsilon**c3 (temperature‑dependent yield offset then hardening)
- Anomalous thermal hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 + c1 * T) * epsilon**c2 (multiplicative strengthening with temperature, e.g., some alloys)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Elastic dominance: stress proportional to strain (σ ∝ ε) for small strains
- Strain hardening exponent: ε**c1 with c1 typically between 0 and 0.5 in metals
- Thermal softening: stress decreases with temperature, often captured by multiplicative factor (1 − c*T) or exp(−c*T)
- Separable constitutive form: σ = f(ε) · g(T) is a common modeling ansatz
- Yield offset: an additive constant term (c0) before strain hardening represents static yield strength
- Strain saturation: at large strains stress tends to a constant (e.g., Voce exponential or rational saturation)
- Temperature‑dependent modulus: E(T) = E₀ − α T leads to σ = (E₀ − α T) · ε for linear‑elastic regime
- Piecewise bilinear: elastic–plastic transition can be smoothed by Ramberg–Osgood or similar power expressions
- Coupled power‑law: σ ∝ ε^n · T^m captures simultaneous influence of strain and temperature
- Exponential thermal decay: exp(−c/T) or exp(−c·T) depending on thermally activated processes

GT Equivalence Verification (MatSci7)

GT: c0*epsilon**c1 - c2*(T - c3) + c4*(T - c5)*log(epsilon + c6)

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the Ground Truth:

**GT:** `6.531*epsilon^3 - 0.687*(T - 289.08) + 3.018*(T - 289.08)*log(epsilon + 1)`

Expanding the GT:
```
= 6.531*epsilon^3 - 0.687*T + 0.687*289.08 + 3.018*T*log(epsilon+1) - 3.018*289.08*log(epsilon+1)
= 6.531*epsilon^3 - 0.687*T + 198.6 + 3.018*T*log(epsilon+1) - 872.8*log(epsilon+1)
```

The GT has these basis functions:
1. `epsilon^3` (polynomial term)
2. `T` (linear in T, constant in epsilon)
3. Constant
4. `T*log(epsilon+1)` (interaction term)
5. `log(epsilon+1)`

So the key structural requirements are: **epsilon^3**, **T**, **T*log(epsilon+1)**, **log(epsilon+1)**, and a **constant**.

Let me check each candidate for the presence of these basis functions, particularly `epsilon^3` and `T*log(epsilon+1)`.

The critical issue is that most candidates use `exp(c*epsilon)`, `sin(c*epsilon)`, or `epsilon/(c+epsilon)` instead of `epsilon^3`. An exponential cannot exactly equal a polynomial for all values. Similarly, `sin` cannot match a polynomial. So I need candidates that can produce both `epsilon^3` and `T*log(epsilon+1)`.

Let me focus on candidates that have:
- A term like `epsilon**c` (with c freely choosable, so c=3)
- A term like `T*log(epsilon+1)` or equivalent

**Candidate 3:** `T*c0*epsilon + c1 + c2*epsilon**c3 + c4*exp(c5*epsilon) + c6*log(c7*epsilon + 1) + c8*epsilon`

This has `epsilon**c3` (set c3=3), `log(c7*epsilon+1)` (set c7=1), but needs `T*log(epsilon+1)`. It only has `T*c0*epsilon`, not `T*log(epsilon+1)`. Setting c5=0 kills the exp. We get: `T*c0*epsilon + c1 + c2*epsilon^3 + c4 + c6*log(epsilon+1) + c8*epsilon`. This gives `T*epsilon` but NOT `T*log(epsilon+1)`. **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 13:** `T*c0 + T*c1*epsilon**c2 + c3 + c4*exp(c5*epsilon) + c6*log(c7*epsilon+1) + c8*epsilon**c2`

Set c2 to make `epsilon**c2 = log(epsilon+1)`? No, that's not a power. But wait - we need `T*log(epsilon+1)`. There's no way to get that from `T*c1*epsilon**c2` since `epsilon**c2` is a power function, not a log. **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 85:** `T*c0 + c1*sin(c2*epsilon+c3) + c4*log(c5*epsilon+1) + c6*epsilon**c7*log(T*c8+1)`

This has `T*log(epsilon+1)` only if `epsilon**c7*log(T*c8+1)` can become `T*log(epsilon+1)`. But `log(T*c8+1) ≠ T` in general. **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 81:** `T*c0 + c1*sin(c2*epsilon+c3) + c4*log(c5*epsilon+1) + c6*epsilon*log(T*c7+1)`

Needs `T*log(epsilon+1)` but has `epsilon*log(T*c7+1)`. These are different. **NO MATCH.**
